{"Quotes": "[1] \"Carbon dioxide is considered as a mild or an unconventional oxidant. Recently, catalytic oxidative dehydrogenation of ethane and propane by carbon dioxide instead of oxygen has been investigated by several groups, and rather high selectivity to corresponding olefins was reported.\"\n\n[2] \"The promoting effect of carbon dioxide on the dehydrogenation reaction can be attributed to the reverse water gas shift reaction, which accelerates the formation of the dehydrogenation products by transforming H2 with CO2 into CO and H2O\"\n\n[3] \"ZSM-5, a typical MFI-type zeolite, has been widely used in the chemical industry. Because of the tri-dimensional micro-pore structure and large specific surface area, the ZSM-5 zeolite is considered to be a good catalyst or support [8,9].\"\n\n[4] \"Ga2O3/HZSM-5 catalysts show better stability than b-Ga2O3, and the higher Si/Al ratio HZSM-5 supported gallium oxide catalysts are more resistant to deactivation.\"\n\n[5] \"The promoting effect of CO2 on the dehydrogenation reaction is attributed to the reverse water gas shift reaction. The catalyst stability is also enhanced by the introduction of CO2.\"\n\n[6] \"The negative effect of CO2 displacement on the reaction is not evident at a low concentration of CO2, and the initial ethane conversion increases with increasing the CO2/C2H6 ratio. When the CO2 concentration increases, this negative effect becomes dominant, and the ethane conversion begins to decrease.\"\n\n[7] \"Meanwhile, CO2 has a negative effect on the reaction by displacement of the ethane adsorbed on the catalyst surface.\"\n\n[8] \"The stability was improved with further increasing in the CO2 partial pressure. The Boudouard reaction (i.e. C + CO2 ! 2CO), which removes the carbon deposit from the catalyst surface and improves the stability of the catalyst, was observed over Ga2O3-loaded catalysts\"", "English": "Although the provided literature does not directly address chromium oxide catalysts, it offers valuable insights into the influence of support materials and reaction conditions on gallium oxide catalysts for CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions. These findings can be extrapolated to provide general principles that may apply to other metal oxide catalysts, including chromium oxide:\n\n1. Support Materials:\n   - HZSM-5 zeolite is an effective support due to its tri-dimensional micro-pore structure and large specific surface area.\n   - Higher Si/Al ratio in HZSM-5 supports leads to improved catalyst stability and resistance to deactivation.\n   - The choice of support significantly impacts catalyst performance, activity, and stability.\n\n2. CO2 Partial Pressure:\n   - CO2 acts as a mild oxidant and plays a complex role in the reaction.\n   - At low concentrations, CO2 promotes the reaction through the reverse water gas shift reaction, removing H2 and driving dehydrogenation forward.\n   - As CO2 concentration increases, it can negatively affect the reaction by displacing adsorbed ethane on the catalyst surface, leading to decreased conversion.\n   - Higher CO2 partial pressures improve catalyst stability by suppressing coke formation through the Boudouard reaction.\n\n3. Activity and Selectivity:\n   - The balance between support acidity and CO2 partial pressure influences both activity and selectivity.\n   - Initial activity may decrease with increasing Si/Al ratio in the support, but stability improves.\n\n4. Stability:\n   - The introduction of CO2 enhances catalyst stability by suppressing coke formation and promoting product desorption.\n   - Higher Si/Al ratio supports and increased CO2 partial pressure contribute to improved catalyst stability.\n\n5. Mechanistic Pathways:\n   - The reverse water gas shift reaction plays a crucial role in promoting dehydrogenation.\n   - Competitive adsorption between CO2 and ethane on catalyst active sites affects reaction kinetics.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs in optimizing overall performance include:\n   - Balancing acidity for high activity while avoiding side reactions and coking.\n   - Optimizing CO2 concentration to promote stability without sacrificing conversion.\n   - Finding the right balance between initial activity (favored by higher acidity) and long-term stability (favored by lower acidity).\n   - Managing the dual role of CO2 as both a promoter and potential inhibitor of the reaction.\n\nWhile these findings are based on gallium oxide catalysts, similar considerations may apply when optimizing chromium oxide catalysts for CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions. However, direct comparisons and specific optimizations for chromium-based systems would require additional research.", "Chinese": "尽管所提供的文献没有直接讨论铬氧化物催化剂，但它为我们提供了关于载体材料和反应条件对氧化镓催化剂在CO2氧化脱氢反应中的影响的有价值见解。这些发现可以推广为一般原则，可能适用于其他金属氧化物催化剂，包括铬氧化物：\n\n1. 载体材料：\n   - HZSM-5沸石由于其三维微孔结构和大比表面积，是一种有效的载体。\n   - HZSM-5载体中较高的Si/Al比导致催化剂稳定性提高和抗失活能力增强。\n   - 载体的选择显著影响催化剂的性能、活性和稳定性。\n\n2. CO2分压：\n   - CO2作为温和的氧化剂，在反应中起着复杂的作用。\n   - 在低浓度时，CO2通过逆水气变换反应促进反应，去除H2并推动脱氢反应向前进行。\n   - 随着CO2浓度的增加，它可能会通过置换催化剂表面吸附的乙烷而对反应产生负面影响，导致转化率下降。\n   - 较高的CO2分压通过布达反应抑制积碳形成，从而提高催化剂稳定性。\n\n3. 活性和选择性：\n   - 载体酸度和CO2分压之间的平衡影响活性和选择性。\n   - 随着载体中Si/Al比的增加，初始活性可能会下降，但稳定性会提高。\n\n4. 稳定性：\n   - CO2的引入通过抑制积碳形成和促进产物脱附来增强催化剂稳定性。\n   - 较高的Si/Al比载体和增加的CO2分压有助于提高催化剂稳定性。\n\n5. 机理路径：\n   - 逆水气变换反应在促进脱氢方面起着关键作用。\n   - CO2和乙烷在催化剂活性位点上的竞争吸附影响反应动力学。\n\n优化整体性能的主要挑战和权衡包括：\n   - 平衡酸度以获得高活性，同时避免副反应和积碳。\n   - 优化CO2浓度以提高稳定性，而不牺牲转化率。\n   - 在初始活性（由较高酸度favored）和长期稳定性（由较低酸度favored）之间找到适当平衡。\n   - 管理CO2作为反应促进剂和潜在抑制剂的双重角色。\n\n虽然这些发现基于氧化镓催化剂，但在优化铬氧化物催化剂用于CO2氧化脱氢反应时，可能会存在类似的考虑因素。然而，对铬基系统进行直接比较和具体优化还需要额外的研究。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.apcata.2008.12.038"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Wang et al. [10] studied the ODH of ethane to ethylene by carbon dioxide over Cr2O3-based catalysts and investigated the effects of different supports on the catalytic activity. As a result, they found that Cr2O3/ZrO2 showed high conversion but low selectivity to ethylene while Cr2O3/TiO2 demonstrated the lowest activity but the highest ethylene selectivity.\"\n\n[2] \"To achieve this, the desired amount of chromium (III) nitrate corresponding to 5 wt.% Cr2O3 in the final product was dissolved in deionized water and then the powdered supports were added under continuous stirring at the same temperature.\"\n\n[3] \"The reactant stream, consisting of 10 vol.% ethane, 50 vol.% carbon dioxide and 40 vol.% nitrogen, was introduced into the reactor at a total flow rate of 75 ml/min. The reaction temperature ranged between 550 and 700 C.\"\n\n[4] \"It has been indicated that CO2 increases the yield of ethylene via a redox mechanism in which the catalyst undergoes reduction by ethane and re-oxidation (by CO2) cycles or reaction coupling between a simple dehydrogenation of ethane and the reverse watergas shift reaction (RWGS)\"\n\n[5] \"In order to improve ethylene selectivity and catalytic activity, it is interesting to use TiO2ZrO2 as a combined support. The mixed oxide nanocomposite catalysts also displayed superior ODH activity than their individual component oxides owing to enhancement in the acid-base bifunctional behavior [22].\"\n\n[6] \"The addition of ZrO2 can prevent TiO2 phase transformations from anatase to rutile at high temperature, thereby promoting the thermal stability of the catalysts [23].\"\n\n[7] \"CO2 is now considered as a soft oxidant in the dehydrogenation of ethane due to its role as a diluent in achieving high equilibrium conversion, enhancing the selectivity to ethylene, and maintaining longer catalyst life time [16,17].\"", "English": "The literature provides insights into how various support materials and reaction conditions influence chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions:\n\n1. Support materials:\n- Different supports significantly affect catalytic activity and selectivity.\n- Cr2O3/ZrO2 showed high conversion but low ethylene selectivity.\n- Cr2O3/TiO2 demonstrated low activity but high ethylene selectivity.\n- TiO2-ZrO2 combined support improved both ethylene selectivity and catalytic activity due to enhanced acid-base bifunctional behavior.\n- ZrO2 addition to TiO2 prevents phase transformations at high temperatures, promoting catalyst thermal stability.\n\n2. Reaction conditions:\n- The study used 5 wt% Cr2O3 loading on supports.\n- Reaction conditions included 50 vol% CO2 partial pressure and temperatures of 550-700°C.\n- CO2 acts as a soft oxidant, helping to achieve high equilibrium conversion, enhance ethylene selectivity, and maintain longer catalyst lifetime.\n\n3. Mechanistic pathways:\n- CO2 increases ethylene yield via a redox mechanism where the catalyst undergoes reduction by ethane and re-oxidation by CO2.\n- Reaction coupling occurs between simple dehydrogenation of ethane and the reverse water-gas shift reaction (RWGS).\n\n4. Challenges and trade-offs:\n- Balancing activity and selectivity is a key challenge, as demonstrated by the different performances of Cr2O3/ZrO2 and Cr2O3/TiO2.\n- Optimizing CO2 partial pressure and temperature to maximize ethylene yield while minimizing side reactions.\n- Maintaining catalyst stability at high temperatures.\n\n5. Optimization strategies:\n- Using combined supports like TiO2-ZrO2 to leverage benefits of individual materials.\n- Tuning CO2 concentration to enhance performance while avoiding catalyst deactivation.\n\nHowever, the literature does not provide comprehensive information on other supports like SiO2, MCM-41, H-ZSM-5, Al2O3, or CeO2. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Cr2O3/ZSM-5 [13], Cr2O3/Al2O3, Cr2O3/SiO2, Cr2O3/ZrO2, Cr2O3/TiO2 [21], modified Cr2O3/ZrO2 nano-composites [4], Cr/SBA-15/Al2O3/FeCrAl monoliths [17], CrO, CrVO oxide [7], Ga incorporated Cr2O3 supported on ZSM-5 and silicalite [18] catalysts have been tried for oxidative dehydrogenation of ethane in presence of CO2.\"\n\n[2] \"Cr2O3/Al2O3 catalyst is seen to exhibit its best catalytic activity with 32 % ethane and 21 % CO2 conversions and an ethylene selectivity of 46 %. Cr2O3/ZrO2 shows higher activity (42 % ethane conversion) but with a decreased ethylene selectivity (36 %).\"\n\n[3] \"The variation in the ODE activity of the chromia-based catalysts is due to the difference in their redox property as revealed by Wang et al. [21]. It is also reported that both Cr2+ and Cr3+ ions have a strong role to play in the catalytic reaction as active sites [6, 21].\"\n\n[4] \"CO2 as an oxidant offers higher ethylene selectivity compared to O2. The reduction in ethylene selectivity during ODE with O2 could be due to secondary oxidation of ethylene.\"\n\n[5] \"CO2 is now considered as a mild oxidant in the dehydrogenation of ethane due to its advantages in containing the exothermicity of the reaction, its role as a diluent in offering high equilibrium conversion, improving the selectivity to ethylene, reducing coke formation and maintaining longer catalyst life time [13, 23].\"\n\n[6] \"The higher basicity of Al2O3 than that of ZrO2 may be the reason for decrease in the activity.\"\n\n[7] \"The conversion of ethane increases with increase in temperature irrespective of the oxidizing agent used in the reaction.\"", "English": "Various support materials (such as ZSM-5, Al2O3, SiO2, ZrO2, and TiO2) significantly influence the activity, selectivity, and stability of chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions. \n\n1. Activity and Selectivity:\n   - Cr2O3/ZrO2 shows higher activity (42% ethane conversion) but lower ethylene selectivity (36%).\n   - Cr2O3/Al2O3 exhibits lower activity (32% ethane conversion) but higher ethylene selectivity (46%).\n   - Mixed oxide supports like Al2O3-ZrO2 offer a balance between activity and selectivity.\n\n2. Redox Properties:\n   - The variation in catalytic activity is attributed to differences in redox properties of the catalysts.\n   - Both Cr2+ and Cr3+ ions play crucial roles as active sites in the catalytic reaction.\n\n3. Support Basicity:\n   - The higher basicity of Al2O3 compared to ZrO2 may contribute to decreased activity.\n\n4. Reaction Conditions:\n   - Temperature: Ethane conversion increases with temperature, regardless of the oxidizing agent.\n   - CO2 as an oxidant:\n     a) Offers higher ethylene selectivity compared to O2.\n     b) Acts as a mild oxidant, containing reaction exothermicity.\n     c) Serves as a diluent, offering high equilibrium conversion.\n     d) Improves ethylene selectivity and reduces coke formation.\n     e) Maintains longer catalyst lifetime.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs:\n1. Balancing activity and selectivity: Higher activity often corresponds to lower ethylene selectivity.\n2. Optimizing support material: Different supports offer varying combinations of activity and selectivity.\n3. Controlling reaction conditions: Temperature and oxidant choice significantly impact performance.\n4. Preventing secondary oxidation: Especially important when using O2 as an oxidant.\n\nThe literature does not provide specific information on the influence of CO2 partial pressure or detailed mechanistic pathways. Further research is needed to fully understand these aspects and to develop catalysts that can overcome the activity-selectivity trade-off.", "Chinese": "各种支持材料（如ZSM-5、Al2O3、SiO2、ZrO2和TiO2）显著影响了铬氧化物催化剂在CO2氧化脱氢反应中的活性、选择性和稳定性。\n\n1. 活性和选择性：\n   - Cr2O3/ZrO2显示出更高的活性（42%乙烷转化率）但乙烯选择性较低（36%）。\n   - Cr2O3/Al2O3表现出较低的活性（32%乙烷转化率）但乙烯选择性较高（46%）。\n   - 混合氧化物支持材料如Al2O3-ZrO2在活性和选择性之间提供了平衡。\n\n2. 氧化还原性质：\n   - 催化活性的变化归因于催化剂氧化还原性质的差异。\n   - Cr2+和Cr3+离子都在催化反应中作为活性位点发挥关键作用。\n\n3. 支持材料碱性：\n   - Al2O3相比ZrO2的较高碱性可能导致活性降低。\n\n4. 反应条件：\n   - 温度：无论使用何种氧化剂，乙烷转化率随温度升高而增加。\n   - CO2作为氧化剂：\n     a) 与O2相比提供更高的乙烯选择性。\n     b) 作为温和的氧化剂，控制反应放热性。\n     c) 作为稀释剂，提供高平衡转化率。\n     d) 提高乙烯选择性并减少积碳形成。\n     e) 维持更长的催化剂寿命。\n\n主要挑战和权衡：\n1. 平衡活性和选择性：较高的活性通常对应较低的乙烯选择性。\n2. 优化支持材料：不同的支持材料提供不同的活性和选择性组合。\n3. 控制反应条件：温度和氧化剂的选择显著影响性能。\n4. 防止二次氧化：特别是在使用O2作为氧化剂时很重要。\n\n文献没有提供关于CO2分压影响或详细反应机理途径的具体信息。需要进一步研究以全面理解这些方面，并开发能够克服活性-选择性权衡的催化剂。", "Doi": "10.1007/s13203-014-0043-4"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"Among these catalysts, chromium-based catalysts have proven to be the most effective catalysts for this reaction [57].\"\n\n[2] \"In order to obtain better catalytic activity, some efforts had been focused on the supports of chromium-based catalysts using TS-1 [11] and MSU-x [12].\"\n\n[3] \"Compared to other Cr2O3-based nano-composite catalysts for the oxidative dehydrogenation of ethane to ethylene with CO2, the Cr2O3/ZrO2 nano-composite catalysts showed high catalytic activity with low selectivity to ethylene in our prior research [15].\"\n\n[4] \"The objective of this work is to attempt to improve the ethylene selectivity in the dehydrogenation of ethane with CO2 on the Cr2O3/ZrO2 nano-composite catalyst with the addition of Fe, Ni, Mn, and Co oxides.\"\n\n[5] \"The ethylene selectivity of the Fe5-Cr10/Zr, Mn5-Cr10/Zr and Co5-Cr10/Zr nano-composite catalysts was markedly higher than that of the Cr2O3/ZrO2 nano-composite catalyst, while their ethane and CO2 conversions were lower than that of the Cr2O3/ZrO2 nano-composite catalyst.\"\n\n[6] \"Among the prepared catalysts, the Fe5-Cr10/Zr nano-composite catalyst exhibited not only high ethylene selectivity, but also relatively high ethane and CO2 conversions.\"\n\n[7] \"The distribution of chromium species, oxygen species and base/acid property on the surface of catalyst cooperatively determined the catalytic activity in dehydrogenations of ethane to ethylene using CO2 as an oxidant.\"\n\n[8] \"Up to now, Fe-Mn/Si-2 [1], La2O3/-Al2O3 [2], Mo2C/SiO2 [4], Cr/H-ZSM-5 [5], K-Cr-Mn/SiO2 [6], Cr/SiO2 [7], Ga/TiO2 [8], CeO2-based [9] and metal oxides [10] catalysts have been used in the dehydrogenation of ethane with CO2 as an oxidant.\"\n\n[9] \"The reactant stream consisting of 20% ethane, 60% carbon dioxide and 20% Ar was introduced into the reactor at a flow rate of 15 ml/min. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Cr oxides exhibit their highest activity and selectivity when supported by materials such as SiO2, siliceous MCM-41 and H-ZSM-5 with high SiO2 content\"\n\n[2] \"The oxidation state of Cr in a CrOx catalyst for the CO2-ODH of C2H6 depends on whether the catalyst is supported on Al2O3, ZrO2, CeO2 or CexZr1xO2\"\n\n[3] \"CrOx/γ-Al2O3 and CrOx/ZrO2 composites exhibit the highest ODHE activities but operate through different pathways. Thus, CrOx/γ-Al2O3 primarily works by the two-step DDE and RWGS mechanism, and can undergo deactivation if cracking affords substantial coke. By contrast, CrOx/ZrO2 performs CO2-ODH in a single step (albeit in competition with DR) and its mode of deactivation involves sintering or conversion into inactive Cr species.\"\n\n[4] \"Studies on the CO2-ODHP (P signifies propane) reaction at 873K concluded that CrOx/SiO2 would exhibit increased activity and C3H6 selectivity with increasing CO2 partial pressure, whereas the activity of CrOx/γ-Al2O3 would decrease with even a slight increase in the CO2 partial pressure\"\n\n[5] \"Increasing the Cr content to 8wt% affords the greatest CrVI:CrIII ratios and increased alkane conversion\"\n\n[6] \"CrVI=O species dehydrogenate alkanes to the respective alkene more quickly than the resulting CrIII species undergo reoxidation by abstracting O from CO2\"\n\n[7] \"Doping the catalyst with Fe, Co or Mn improved C2H4 selectivity because the presence of the metals increases the concentration of weakly acidic sites that facilitate C2H6 activation. Moreover, doping leads to a decrease in the number of strong acid sites that mediate reforming and cracking\"", "English": "The influence of support materials and reaction conditions on chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions is significant:\n\n1. Support materials:\n- SiO2, MCM-41, and H-ZSM-5 with high SiO2 content provide the highest activity and selectivity.\n- Al2O3, ZrO2, and CeO2 supports affect the oxidation state of Cr, leading to different reaction pathways and deactivation mechanisms.\n- CrOx/γ-Al2O3 operates via a two-step mechanism (DDE and RWGS) and is prone to coking.\n- CrOx/ZrO2 performs single-step CO2-ODH but competes with dry reforming and deactivates through sintering or conversion to inactive Cr species.\n\n2. Reaction kinetics:\n- CrVI=O species dehydrogenate alkanes faster than CrIII species are reoxidized by CO2, leading to eventual deactivation.\n\n5. Doping:\n- Adding Fe, Co, or Mn improves C2H4 selectivity by increasing weakly acidic sites and decreasing strong acid sites.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs in optimizing overall performance include:\n1. {"Quotes": "[1] \"To prepare the 5wt% of Cr2O3/ZrO2 catalyst by precipitation method, ZrO2 (Alfa-Aesor, 90m2/g, 99%) was pre-heated at 600 for 6 hour before being grinded and sieved to 125μm in particle size.\"\n\n[2] \"The results with different mole fractions of C3H8 were displayed with solid symbols and the conclusion drawn from the data in these figures is an inhibition of C3H8 conversion, but also an improvement in C3H6 selectivity.\"\n\n[3] \"It was shown that the increase of C3H8 partial pressure is highly beneficial for the enhancement of C3H6 selectivity. {"Quotes": "[1] \"It was found that the nature of support strongly effects on the catalytic performance in the dehydrogenation with CO2. Over the CrOx/SiO2 catalyst CO2 enhance the propene yield, whereas over the CrOx/Al2O3 catalyst the yield and selectivity of propene in the presence of CO2 strongly decrease.\"\n\n[2] \"The catalytic properties of the supported chromium catalysts are strongly affected by the acidity/basicity of the oxide support. SiO2 supports enhance propene yield in the presence of CO2, while Al2O3 supports decrease both yield and selectivity. This difference is attributed to the acidity/basicity of the support materials.\n\nThe basicity of Al2O3 is proposed to cause the poisonous effect of CO2 on dehydrogenation activity. Additionally, CO2 and/or steam formed during the reaction may alter the acidity/basicity of the CrOx/Al2O3 catalyst surface, further affecting its performance.\n\nChromium loading levels also impact catalyst performance. For CrOx/SiO2 catalysts, increasing chromium content leads to a greater promoting effect of CO2. Conversely, for CrOx/Al2O3 catalysts, higher chromium loading reduces the poisoning effect of CO2.\n\nThe key challenges in optimizing overall performance include balancing the acidity/basicity of the support material, managing the effects of CO2 and steam on the catalyst surface, and determining the optimal chromium loading for each support type. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Recently, attempts have been made to utilize less reactive carbon dioxide as an oxidant for dehydrogenation of ethane to yield ethene [14, 15]. The advantage of utilization of the green house gas CO2 as oxidant is that it might lead to higher selectivity at elevated temperatures because it is less prone to supply oxygen species for reaction.\"\n\n[2] \"Up to date, Mo2C/SiO2 [17], Cr/H-ZSM-5 [18, 19], Cr/TS-1[20], Cr/SiO2 [15], Ga/TiO2 [21], and CeO2-based oxides [22] have been used in the dehydrogenation of ethane with CO2 as an oxidant. Among these catalysts, chromium-based catalysts have proven to be the most active for this reaction.\"\n\n[3] \"Chromium based catalysts supported on TS-1 or Cr/H-ZSM-5 show best performance, but their reaction temperature is limited to about 650 C, since at higher temperatures selectivity decreases significantly [20].\"\n\n[4] \"The dependence of ethane conversion and selectivity to ethene on the ratio CO2/C2H6 is shown in Fig. 5. It shows that in the absence of CO2 the selectivity was 78% and it increased to >97% with increasing CO2/C2H6 ratio up to 1.5. Further increase in CO2 did not show significant effect.\"\n\n[5] \"The role of CO2 is to generate oxygen species that take part in the formation of ethene as well as to suppress carbon deposition.\"\n\n[6] \"5%Cr/TS-1 showed a consistent conversion of CO2. Interestingly, selectivity to CO significantly exceeded 100%. This could happen probably due to some deep oxidation of hydrocarbons (ethane, ethene) to CO resulting in an apparent selectivity to CO higher than 100%.\"", "English": "The literature provides insights into how support materials and reaction conditions influence chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions:\n\n1. Chromium-based catalysts, particularly those supported on TS-1 or H-ZSM-5, have shown the best performance among the studied catalysts.\n\n2. Activity and selectivity: Chromium-based catalysts are the most active for this reaction. The use of CO2 as an oxidant can lead to higher selectivity at elevated temperatures compared to stronger oxidants, as it is less prone to supply oxygen species for undesired side reactions.\n\n3. Temperature: Chromium-based catalysts supported on TS-1 or H-ZSM-5 show optimal performance at temperatures up to about 650°C. At higher temperatures, selectivity decreases significantly.\n\n4. CO2 partial pressure: Increasing the CO2/C2H6 ratio up to 1.5 led to improved selectivity to ethene, from 78% without CO2 to >97% with CO2. Further increases in CO2 concentration did not significantly affect the performance.\n\n5. Mechanistic pathways: CO2 generates oxygen species that participate in ethene formation and suppress carbon deposition. For Cr-based catalysts, ethene formation occurs through the reduction of Cr(VI) species, while CO2 dissociates to re-oxidize Cr(III) to Cr(VI).\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs include:\n- Balancing activity and selectivity, as higher temperatures increase activity but may decrease selectivity.\n- Optimizing the CO2/C2H6 ratio to achieve high selectivity without unnecessarily diluting the reactants.\n- Managing deep oxidation of hydrocarbons to CO, which can affect the apparent selectivity.\n- Developing catalysts that maintain high selectivity at higher temperatures to improve overall performance.\n\nThe literature does not provide comprehensive information on all the support materials mentioned in the question (e.g., MCM-41, Al2O3, ZrO2) or detailed analysis of catalyst stability. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Ga2O3/TiO2, Ga2O3/Al2O3, and Ga2O3/ZrO2 are better catalysts for the dehydrogenation reaction than Ga2O3/SiO2 and Ga2O3/MgO, because they contain many more acid sites of medium to strong and strong strength on the surface.\"\n\n[2] \"CO2 has a promoting effect on dehydrogenation activity over Ga2O3/TiO2 but a negative effect over Ga2O3/ZrO2 and Ga2O3/Al2O3. "English": "The literature provides some insights into the influence of support materials and reaction conditions on chromium oxide catalysts for CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions, although not comprehensively:\n\n1. Catalyst types: Cr2O3-based catalysts are among the most frequently reported for propane dehydrogenation (PDH) with CO2.\n\n2. Reaction mechanism: Cr2O3-based catalysts follow a one-step pathway mechanism consistent with the Mars-Van Krevelen mechanism.\n\n3. Support effects: \n   - The choice of support material plays a crucial role in the dispersion and electronic properties of the active species, which can further tune the catalytic performance.\n   - Acid-base properties of supports strongly affect the selectivity to propylene.\n   - Higher dispersion of active species on the support is favorable for propylene production.\n\n4. Reaction conditions:\n   - CO2 serves multiple functions: as a milder oxidant, heat supplier for endothermic reactions, diluent for enhancing equilibrium conversion, and agent for coke removal.\n\n5. Challenges:\n   - Fast deactivation due to exhaustion of active lattice oxygen atoms or coke deposition is a common problem.\n\n6. Performance optimization:\n   - Balanced acidic/basic properties and high dispersion of active species are essential for achieving high catalytic performance.\n   - Synergy between dehydrogenation and reverse water gas shift reactions is important.\n\nThe literature does not provide specific information on how different supports (SiO2, MCM-41, H-ZSM-5, Al2O3, ZrO2, and CeO2) affect chromium oxide catalysts' performance or how CO2 partial pressure influences the reaction. More targeted research would be needed to fully address these aspects and the specific challenges and trade-offs in optimizing chromium oxide catalysts for CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions.", "Chinese": "文献对铬氧化物催化剂在CO2氧化脱氢反应中的载体材料和反应条件的影响提供了一些见解，尽管不够全面：\n\n1. 催化剂类型：Cr2O3基催化剂是CO2存在下丙烷脱氢（PDH）反应中最常报道的催化剂之一。\n\n2. 反应机理：Cr2O3基催化剂遵循与Mars-Van Krevelen机理一致的单步反应路径机制。\n\n3. 载体效应：\n   - 载体材料的选择对活性物种的分散和电子性质起着关键作用，这可以进一步调节催化性能。\n   - 载体的酸碱性质强烈影响丙烯的选择性。\n   - 活性物种在载体上的高度分散有利于丙烯的生产。\n\n4. 反应条件：\n   - CO2具有多重功能：作为更温和的氧化剂，为吸热反应提供热量，作为稀释剂增强平衡转化，以及作为去除积碳的试剂。\n\n5. 挑战：\n   - 由于活性晶格氧原子耗尽或积碳沉积导致的快速失活是一个常见问题。\n\n6. 性能优化：\n   - 平衡的酸碱性质和活性物种的高度分散对于实现高催化性能至关重要。\n   - 脱氢反应和逆水气变换反应之间的协同作用很重要。\n\n该文献没有提供关于不同载体（SiO2、MCM-41、H-ZSM-5、Al2O3、ZrO2和CeO2）如何影响铬氧化物催化剂性能的具体信息，也没有说明CO2分压如何影响反应。要全面解答这些方面以及优化铬氧化物催化剂用于CO2氧化脱氢反应的具体挑战和权衡，需要进行更有针对性的研究。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.apcata.2011.08.018"},

{"Quotes": "\"Several factors influence the concentration of these species on the surface of supports. They include the type of the Cr precursor, preparation conditions (e.g., calcination temperature), Cr content and properties of the support (e.g. isoelectric point, specific surface area).\"\n\n\"Up to now, a number of mesoporous catalysts with different pore architecture prepared by one-pot and post synthesis techniques have been investigated as the potential catalysts for dehydrogenation of propane to propene in the presence of CO2\"\n\n\"The role of CO2 in the dehydrogenation of hydrocarbons such as propane, over chromium oxide-based catalysts, is to enhance the yield of propene and the stability of the catalyst. The promoting role of CO2 is attributed mainly to its weak oxidative properties.\"\n\n\"CO2 participates in the process as an oxidant and allows for regeneration of the reduced chromium sites generated during the dehydrogenation of propane\"\n\n\"Up to now several cycles between various redox Cr species including Cr6+/Cr3+, Cr5+/Cr3+, and Cr3+/Cr2+ have been proposed.\"\n\n\"The high-surface-area supports provide more adsorption sites which may stabilize the redox Cr species.\"\n\n\"Regardless of the oxidation state of Cr species which participate in the redox mechanism, it is clear from the above that for the activation of CO2 in the oxidative pathway, high-valent redox chromium species (Cr6+, Cr5+ and Cr3+) are needed.\"\n\n\"Because of the fact that in reaction conditions CO2 is reduced to CO, together with hydrogen (synthesis gas) or separately, it has many applications in the chemical industry.\"\n\n\"In addition, it is known that the reverse watergas shift reaction (RWGS) can proceed over redox and nonredox Cr sites [18,23,39]. This reaction enhances the yield of propene by consumption of hydrogen which is produced in the nonoxidative pathway (in equilibrium propane dehydrogenation, Scheme 1).\"", "English": "The activity, selectivity, stability, and mechanistic pathways of chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions are influenced by various support materials and reaction conditions:\n\n1. Support materials: High-surface-area mesoporous supports (e.g., SBA-1, MCM-41, SBA-15) provide more adsorption sites to stabilize redox Cr species, leading to better catalytic performance. These supports allow for higher Cr dispersion and delayed formation of less active Cr2O3 crystallites compared to traditional supports.\n\n2. Preparation methods: One-pot and post-synthesis techniques affect the pore architecture and Cr distribution. Factors like Cr precursor type, calcination temperature, and Cr content influence the concentration and nature of active species on the support surface.\n\n3. CO2 partial pressure: Higher CO2 concentration enhances propene yield and catalyst stability. CO2 acts as a weak oxidizing agent, helping to regenerate reduced chromium sites and shift the equilibrium towards dehydrogenation products.\n\n4. Reaction mechanisms: Various redox cycles (Cr6+/Cr3+, Cr5+/Cr3+, Cr3+/Cr2+) have been proposed. High-valent redox chromium species (Cr6+, Cr5+, Cr3+) are crucial for CO2 activation in the oxidative pathway.\n\n5. Activity and selectivity: The activity depends on the concentration of high-valent redox Cr species. Selectivity to propene is generally high (85-93%) for chromium catalysts on mesoporous supports.\n\n6. Stability: CO2 improves catalyst stability by suppressing coke formation. However, higher CO2 concentrations can lead to faster catalyst darkening due to increased propene reactivity.\n\n7. Side reactions: The reverse water-gas shift reaction (RWGS) occurs over both redox and non-redox Cr sites, enhancing propene yield by consuming hydrogen produced in the non-oxidative pathway.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs in optimizing overall performance include:\n\n1. Balancing Cr loading to maximize active species while avoiding formation of less active Cr2O3 crystallites.\n2. Optimizing CO2 concentration to enhance propene yield and stability without accelerating catalyst deactivation.\n3. Developing supports that provide high surface area and thermal stability while maintaining accessibility to active sites.\n4. Understanding and controlling the complex redox mechanisms to improve catalyst design.\n5. Minimizing irreversible deactivation caused by loss of redox Cr species or pore structure collapse during multiple reaction-regeneration cycles.\n6. Balancing activity/selectivity with long-term stability, as conditions promoting high conversion may also accelerate deactivation.", "Chinese": "在CO2氧化脱氢反应中，各种载体材料和反应条件影响铬氧化物催化剂的活性、选择性、稳定性和机理途径：\n\n1. 载体材料：高比表面积的介孔载体（如SBA-1、MCM-41、SBA-15）提供更多吸附位点来稳定氧化还原铬物种，从而带来更好的催化性能。与传统载体相比，这些载体允许更高的铬分散度，并延迟了活性较低的Cr2O3晶体的形成。\n\n2. 制备方法：一锅法和后合成技术影响孔道结构和铬分布。铬前驱体类型、焙烧温度和铬含量等因素影响载体表面活性物种的浓度和性质。\n\n3. CO2分压：较高的CO2浓度可提高丙烯产率和催化剂稳定性。CO2作为弱氧化剂，有助于再生还原的铬位点，并将平衡向脱氢产物方向移动。\n\n4. 反应机理：已提出多种氧化还原循环（Cr6+/Cr3+、Cr5+/Cr3+、Cr3+/Cr2+）。高价态氧化还原铬物种（Cr6+、Cr5+、Cr3+）对CO2在氧化途径中的活化至关重要。\n\n5. 活性和选择性：活性取决于高价态氧化还原铬物种的浓度。对于介孔载体上的铬催化剂，丙烯的选择性通常很高（85-93%）。\n\n6. 稳定性：CO2通过抑制积碳形成来提高催化剂稳定性。然而，较高的CO2浓度可能由于丙烯反应性增加而导致催化剂变黑速度加快。\n\n7. 副反应：逆水气变换反应（RWGS）在氧化还原和非氧化还原铬位点上进行，通过消耗非氧化途径产生的氢气来增加丙烯产率。\n\n优化整体性能的主要挑战和权衡包括：\n\n1. 平衡铬负载量，以最大化活性物种，同时避免形成活性较低的Cr2O3晶体。\n2. 优化CO2浓度，以提高丙烯产率和稳定性，同时不加速催化剂失活。\n3. 开发提供高比表面积和热稳定性的载体，同时保持活性位点的可接近性。\n4. 理解和控制复杂的氧化还原机制，以改进催化剂设计。\n5. 最小化在多次反应-再生循环过程中由于氧化还原铬物种损失或孔结构崩塌导致的不可逆失活。\n6. 平衡活性/选择性和长期稳定性，因为促进高转化率的条件也可能加速失活。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.micromeso.2012.05.011"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"The effect of CO2 on the activity for the dehydrogenation of C3H8 over Cr/SiO2 and Cr/Al2O3 prepared by impregnation method was investigated.\"\n\n[2] \"The activity of Cr/SiO2 was enhanced with increasing the partial pressure of CO2, while the activity of Cr/Al2O3 was remarkably reduced by the addition of a small amount of CO2.\"\n\n[3] \"Kinetic analysis suggested that CO2 adsorbed on Al2O3 inhibited the adsorption of C3H8, and that CO2 reduced the activity of Cr/Al2O3.\"\n\n[4] \"Cr K-edge XAFS spectra and TPR profiles indicated that the redox cycle between Cr(III)O6 and Cr(VI)O4 had an important role in the dehydrogenation of C3H6 over both Cr/SiO2 and Cr/Al2O3 regardless of the support.\"\n\n[5] \"CO2 could oxidize a part of Cr(III) species to Cr(VI) species under the reaction condition. Support material influence:\n- Cr/SiO2 showed enhanced activity with increasing CO2 partial pressure.\n- Cr/Al2O3 exhibited reduced activity with the addition of even small amounts of CO2.\n\n2. Reaction conditions (CO2 partial pressure):\n- Increasing CO2 partial pressure enhanced the activity of Cr/SiO2.\n- Even small amounts of CO2 remarkably reduced the activity of Cr/Al2O3.\n\n3. Support materials: MCM-41 was found to be the most effective support among those tested. Cr-MCM-41 showed the highest activity for propane dehydrogenation, with 30% conversion and over 90% selectivity to propene. In contrast, Cr/Cab-O-Sil and Cr/SiO2 showed lower activities and poorer regeneration capabilities.\n\n2. CO2 partial pressure: Increasing CO2 partial pressure led to increased rates of propene and CO formation, while H2 formation remained relatively constant. This suggests that CO2 plays a role in shifting the reaction equilibrium and possibly in catalyst regeneration.\n\n3. Reaction mechanism: The active species appears to be tetrahedral Cr(VI)O4, which is reduced to octahedral Cr(III)O6 during the reaction. CO2 can regenerate the active Cr(VI)O4 species, though less efficiently than oxygen.\n\n4. Catalyst stability and regeneration: Cr-MCM-41 showed better stability and regeneration capability compared to Cr/Cab-O-Sil and Cr/SiO2. After O2 treatment, Cr-MCM-41 fully recovered its activity, while Cr/Cab-O-Sil showed no recovery and Cr/SiO2 showed only partial recovery.\n\n5. Reaction conditions: A gas mixture of N2:CO2:C3H8 at 10:34:6 molar ratio resulted in 17% propane conversion and 15.9% propene yield for Cr-MCM-41-DHT.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs include:\n- Balancing catalyst activity with stability and regeneration capability\n- Optimizing CO2 partial pressure to enhance propene formation while minimizing coke formation\n- Designing catalysts that maintain the active Cr(VI)O4 species during reaction conditions\n- Developing supports that facilitate the redox cycle of chromium species while resisting deactivation\n\nThe main trade-offs involve maximizing propene yield and selectivity while minimizing catalyst deactivation and coke formation. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Wang et al. [9] investigated the effect of support such as Al2O3, SiO2, TiO2 and ZrO2 on the catalytic ODH of ethane to ethylene by CO2 over several supported Cr2O3 catalysts. 8 wt% Cr2O3/SiO2 catalysts could produce a 61% ethane conversion and 55.5% ethylene yield.\"\n\n[2] \"The distribution of Cr2O3 on the supports and surface chromium species structure, which determined the activity of catalysts, was influenced by the nature of supports.\"\n\n[3] \"It is well known that the dispersion, the oxidation state and the structural features of supported species may strongly depend on the support.\"\n\n[4] \"Cr species formed in high oxidation state were reduced during the reaction. It was proposed that these high-valent Cr species were responsible for the high activities of catalysts.\"\n\n[5] \"The catalysts were prone to deactivate in the reaction but could be partially regenerated by oxygen.\"\n\n[6] \"It has been generally recognized that the surface chromium species strongly depends on the surface density of chromium oxide [27].\"\n\n[7] \"When Cr loading was 8 wt%, the diffraction peaks of crystalline α-Cr2O3 appeared in the XRD patterns (Fig. 5B). The color of catalysts changes from yellow to green with the growing of Cr content is in accordance with above phenomenon, indicating the formation of Cr(III) at high loadings of Cr.\"\n\n[8] \"Both Cr-MSU-1 and Cr/MSU-1 exhibited higher activities at the beginning of reaction. As the reactions proceeded, conversions of ethane and CO2 gave a visible drop, suggesting catalysts were deactivated to some degree.\"\n\n[9] \"Cr(VI) acted as active species in the catalysts for initial high activity and the reduction of Cr(VI) to Cr(III) during the reaction resulted in deactivation of catalyst. Support materials: Different supports (Al2O3, SiO2, TiO2, ZrO2) significantly affect the distribution, dispersion, oxidation state, and structural features of chromium species, which in turn influence catalyst activity and performance. SiO2-supported Cr2O3 catalysts showed good performance, with 8 wt% Cr2O3/SiO2 achieving 61% ethane conversion and 55.5% ethylene yield.\n\n2. Chromium loading: The surface chromium species strongly depend on the surface density of chromium oxide. Higher Cr loading (8 wt%) led to the formation of crystalline α-Cr2O3, indicating a change in the oxidation state from Cr(VI) to Cr(III) at higher loadings.\n\n3. Oxidation state: High-valent Cr species (Cr6+ and Cr5+) are responsible for high catalytic activity. However, these species are reduced during the reaction, leading to catalyst deactivation.\n\n4. Stability and deactivation: Catalysts tend to deactivate during the reaction due to the reduction of high-valent Cr species. Both Cr-MSU-1 and Cr/MSU-1 catalysts showed higher initial activities but experienced deactivation over time.\n\n5. Regeneration: Partial regeneration of the catalysts is possible through oxygen or air treatment, suggesting that maintaining the Cr(VI) oxidation state is crucial for catalyst performance. The extent of recovery depends on the support material, with Cr-MSU-1 showing better recovery compared to Cr/MSU-1.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs in optimizing overall performance include:\n\n1. Balancing Cr loading to maximize active sites while preventing the formation of less active crystalline Cr2O3.\n2. Maintaining the Cr(VI) oxidation state during the reaction to prevent deactivation.\n3. Developing effective regeneration strategies to restore catalyst activity.\n4. Optimizing support materials to enhance Cr2O3 distribution, stability, and regeneration efficiency.\n5. Balancing high initial activity with long-term stability, as the highly active Cr6+ species are prone to reduction and deactivation.\n\nThe literature does not provide specific information on the effects of CO2 partial pressure or detailed mechanistic pathways for different supports. {"Quotes": "1. \"Various promoters have been used to further improve catalytic performance. In our prior work, (14-16) it has been demonstrated that Fe-promoted Cr2O3/ZrO2 catalysts exhibit high catalytic activity.\"\n\n2. \"The catalysts, which were prepared by the coprecipitation and coprecipitationimpregnation methods, have the same loadings of Fe and Cr (5 wt % of Fe and 10 wt % of Cr).\"\n\n3. \"The ethylene yield on FeCr/ZrO2 (C) dramatically drops from 50% to 38% over the time on stream. Support material: ZrO2 is used as the support, with Fe-promoted Cr2O3/ZrO2 catalysts showing high catalytic activity.\n\n2. Preparation methods: Two methods (coprecipitation and coprecipitation-impregnation) were compared. The coprecipitation-impregnation method resulted in better stability and higher CO2 conversion, while the coprecipitation method led to higher ethylene selectivity.\n\n3. While not explicitly studied, the high CO2 concentration (60%) suggests a relatively high CO2 partial pressure was used, likely impacting reaction kinetics and pathways.\n\n5. Stability: The coprecipitation-impregnation method produced more stable catalysts, with little variation in ethylene yield over time. In contrast, the coprecipitation method led to a significant drop in ethylene yield.\n\n6. Selectivity vs. Conversion: There appears to be a trade-off between ethylene selectivity and CO2 conversion. The coprecipitation method resulted in higher ethylene selectivity but lower CO2 conversion, while the opposite was true for the coprecipitation-impregnation method.\n\n7. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Most studies in the field of ODH of light paraffins in the presence of CO2 or CO2/O2 mixtures were devoted to ethane [7 21], while ODH of C3C4-alkanes was explored in a lower extent [17,2229].\"\n\n[2] \"Alkaline-earth, transition and rare-earth metal oxides have been tested as catalysts for ODH of C2C4 in the presence of CO2, but the best performance has been obtained with chromium supported on various oxides, zeolites, active carbon and diamond.\"\n\n[3] \"Among the supported systems the most promising results were obtained for SiO2 [12,15,17,21,23,24], also in a mesoporous form [17,27,28], and diamond [22] loaded with 1.78.0 wt% Cr.\"\n\n[4] \"DR UVvis studies indicated that Cr(VI) ions in the form of mono-, di- and polychromates were present in all catalysts, while Cr(III) oxide (a-Cr2O3) was found only for Cr loading higher than 3.0 wt%.\"\n\n[5] \"The catalyst activity seemed correlated to more dispersed chromates.\"\n\n[6] \"Introduction of oxygen in the reaction mixture up to 5.0 vol.% resulted in a significant increase of catalysts activity and stability. Balancing activity and selectivity for specific products.\n\nThe literature does not provide specific information on the influence of CO2 partial pressure or detailed comparisons between all mentioned support materials (e.g., MCM-41, H-ZSM-5, Al2O3, ZrO2, and CeO2). Further research would be needed to fully address these aspects and optimize overall catalyst performance.", "Chinese": "文献提供了关于各种载体材料和反应条件如何影响二氧化碳氧化脱氢反应中的铬氧化物催化剂的见解：\n\n载体材料：\n- 在测试的各种载体中（包括氧化物、分子筛和活性炭），SiO2（包括介孔形式）和金刚石显示出最有前景的结果。\n- 最佳铬负载范围为1.7-8.0 wt%，其中5.0 wt%表现出最高的活性、选择性和稳定性。\n\n反应条件：\n- 向反应混合物中添加氧气（最高5.0 vol%）显著提高了催化剂的活性和稳定性。\n- 这导致丙烯和异丁烯的选择性略有下降，但由于对轻质烯烃的选择性提高，总烯烃选择性增加。\n\n机理见解：\n- 所有催化剂中都存在以单铬酸盐、双铬酸盐和多铬酸盐形式的Cr(VI)离子。\n- 只有在较高的铬负载量（>3.0 wt%）下才形成Cr(III)氧化物。\n- 催化剂活性与更分散的铬酸盐物种相关。\n\n主要挑战和权衡：\n1. 平衡铬负载量，以优化分散性和活性，同时避免Cr(III)氧化物的形成。\n2. 在添加氧气时，管理活性/稳定性增加与潜在选择性损失之间的权衡。\n3. 优化载体材料以增强催化剂性能。\n4. 平衡特定产品的活性和选择性。\n\n文献没有提供关于CO2分压影响的具体信息，也没有详细比较所有提到的载体材料（如MCM-41、H-ZSM-5、Al2O3、ZrO2和CeO2）。需要进行进一步研究以全面解决这些方面并优化催化剂的整体性能。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.apcata.2008.05.037"},
{"Quotes": "\"Wang et al.67 investigated a comparative study on the dehydrogenation of ethane with carbon dioxide over chromium oxide supported on silica, alumina, zirconia and titania to understand the support effect on the catalytic activity.\"\n\n\"Among all the supports, Cr2O3 supported on SiO2 exhibited the highest conversion of ethane, the best ethylene selectivity and the best stability. The following order of activity was observed in the oxidative dehydrogenation of ethane with CO2: Cr2O3/SiO2 > Cr2O3/ZrO2 > Cr2O3/Al2O3 > Cr2O3/TiO2.\"\n\n\"The XRD patterns of these catalysts were unable to distinguish between the phases of Cr2O3 on the supports as no peak corresponding to Cr2O3 was observed due to its fine dispersion.\"\n\n\"The XPS measurements showed that the oxidation states of Cr2O3 over the supports were Cr3+ and Cr6+ ,with slight differences in the Cr6+/Cr3+ ratios.\"\n\n\"Sloczynski et al.69 suggested that the catalytic performance of supported Cr2O3 was better due to the lower reoxidation rate of the supported chromium oxide catalysts as compared with pure chromia, which may be due to the lower surface concentration of the Cr3+ centers on which adsorption of the CO2 molecule takes place.\"\n\n\"Moreover, the Cr6+O bond energy is higher for the supported catalyst than for unsupported chromia due to the presence of Cr6+OM bonds, which are stronger than Cr6+OCr6+ in unsupported Cr2O3.\"\n\n\"The effect of the mole ratio of carbon dioxide to ethylbenzene over Li, Na and K showed a strong increase in the yield of styrene with an increase in the amount of CO2 in the reaction mixture until the CO2/ethyl benzene ratio was 10. A further increase in the ratio above this value decreased the yield.\"", "English": "Support materials significantly influence the activity, selectivity, stability, and mechanistic pathways of chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions:\n\n1. Activity order: Cr2O3/SiO2 > Cr2O3/ZrO2 > Cr2O3/Al2O3 > Cr2O3/TiO2\n2. SiO2 support provides the highest ethane conversion, best ethylene selectivity, and best stability.\n3. Fine dispersion of Cr2O3 on supports, with Cr existing in both Cr3+ and Cr6+ oxidation states.\n4. Supported catalysts perform better than unsupported Cr2O3 due to:\n   - Lower reoxidation rates\n   - Lower surface concentration of Cr3+ sites for CO2 adsorption\n   - Stronger Cr6+-O-M bonds compared to Cr6+-O-Cr6+ in pure Cr2O3\n\nReaction conditions, particularly CO2 partial pressure, play a crucial role:\n- Increasing CO2 concentration improves yields up to an optimal ratio (CO2/reactant = 10)\n- Further increase in CO2 ratio decreases yield\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs in optimizing performance include:\n1. Balancing Cr dispersion and Cr6+/Cr3+ ratio on different supports\n2. Optimizing reducibility of Cr species for redox cycles while maintaining stability\n3. Tuning support properties to influence CO2 activation and product selectivity\n4. Managing coke formation and catalyst deactivation\n5. Balancing CO2 activation with preventing excessive surface adsorption at higher pressures\n\nThe mechanistic pathways are influenced by the nature of the support, affecting the oxidation state, dispersion, and reducibility of chromium species. This impacts CO2 activation, oxygen mobility, and the redox cycle crucial for the dehydrogenation process.", "Chinese": "载体材料显著影响了铬氧化物催化剂在CO2氧化脱氢反应中的活性、选择性、稳定性和机理途径：\n\n1. 活性顺序：Cr2O3/SiO2 > Cr2O3/ZrO2 > Cr2O3/Al2O3 > Cr2O3/TiO2\n2. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Supported chromium oxides are well known to be active catalysts for hydrogenation, isomerization of olefins, and dehydrogenation of alkanes\"\n\n[2] \"The catalytic properties of the supported chromium catalysts are strongly affected by the acidity/basicity of the oxide support.\"\n\n[3] \"Cr2O3/SiO2 shows the highest ethane conversion, while Cr2O3/TiO2 demonstrates the lowest activity, even lower than that of the unsupported Cr2O3 catalyst. Cr2O3/SiO2 also exhibits the highest ethylene selectivity, whereas Cr2O3/ZrO2 gives the lowest selectivity to ethylene.\"\n\n[4] \"Based on the ethane conversion and ethylene yield, the catalytic activity of Cr2O3 and the supported catalysts follows the order of Cr2O3/SiO2 > 5 wt.% Cr2O3/ZrO2 > 5 wt.% Cr2O3/Al2O3 ≈ Cr2O3 > 5 wt.% Cr2O3/TiO2.\"\n\n[5] \"The acidbase property of supports plays an important role in Cr anchorage and dispersion on oxide supports\"\n\n[6] \"It is believed that surface Cr3+ species and Cr6+/Cr3+ couples will be the active sites for dehydrogenation of ethane, based on XPS and TPR measurements. The catalytic activity is dependent on the redox property of catalysts.\"\n\n[7] \"The effect of Cr2O3 loading in Cr2O3/SiO2 system on catalytic activity was investigated; the results are shown in Fig. 1. As seen, ethane conversion increases as Cr2O3 content increases and it reaches the maximum value at 8 wt.% Cr2O3.\"\n\n[8] \"The catalytic stability of Cr2O3/SiO2 catalysts was also investigated at 650°C. Fig. 2 shows the catalytic performance of 5 wt.% Cr2O3/SiO2 and 8 wt.% Cr2O3/SiO2 catalysts as a function of time. It is seen that the two catalysts exhibit deactivation at different rates, which can be ascribed to the carbon deposition.\"\n\n[9] \"The dehydrogenation and oxidative dehydrogenation due to the introduction of CO2 and its decomposition to produce surface oxygen species will be the parallel reaction paths in the dehydrogenation of ethane by carbon dioxide.\"", "English": "The support materials significantly influence the activity, selectivity, stability, and mechanistic pathways of chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions:\n\n1. Activity: The catalytic activity follows the order Cr2O3/SiO2 > Cr2O3/ZrO2 > Cr2O3/Al2O3 ≈ Cr2O3 > Cr2O3/TiO2. SiO2-supported catalysts show the highest ethane conversion, while TiO2-supported catalysts demonstrate the lowest activity.\n\n2. Selectivity: Cr2O3/SiO2 exhibits the highest ethylene selectivity, while Cr2O3/ZrO2 gives the lowest selectivity to ethylene.\n\n3. Stability: Catalysts show deactivation over time due to carbon deposition, with different deactivation rates observed for different Cr2O3 loadings.\n\n4. Cr2O3 loading: For SiO2-supported catalysts, ethane conversion increases with Cr2O3 content, reaching a maximum at 8 wt.% Cr2O3.\n\n5. Support properties: The acidity/basicity of the oxide support strongly affects the catalytic properties, playing an important role in Cr anchorage and dispersion.\n\n6. Active sites and mechanism: Surface Cr3+ species and Cr6+/Cr3+ couples are believed to be the active sites for ethane dehydrogenation. The catalytic activity depends on the redox properties of the catalysts.\n\n7. Reaction pathways: The reaction involves both dehydrogenation and oxidative dehydrogenation pathways due to the introduction of CO2.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs in optimizing overall performance include:\n- Balancing activity and selectivity, as exemplified by Cr2O3/ZrO2 showing high activity but low selectivity.\n- Optimizing Cr2O3 loading to maximize conversion while maintaining stability.\n- Mitigating catalyst deactivation due to carbon deposition.\n- Tailoring the redox properties and acidity/basicity of the catalysts to enhance performance.\n- Managing the parallel reaction pathways (dehydrogenation and oxidative dehydrogenation) for desired product distribution.\n\nThe influence of CO2 partial pressure is not directly addressed in the given literature, which represents a gap in the available data for fully optimizing these catalysts.", "Chinese": "支撑材料显著影响了铬氧化物催化剂在CO2氧化脱氢反应中的活性、选择性、稳定性和机理途径：\n\n1. 活性：催化活性顺序为Cr2O3/SiO2 > Cr2O3/ZrO2 > Cr2O3/Al2O3 ≈ Cr2O3 > Cr2O3/TiO2。SiO2负载的催化剂显示出最高的乙烷转化率，而TiO2负载的催化剂活性最低。\n\n2. 选择性：Cr2O3/SiO2表现出最高的乙烯选择性，而Cr2O3/ZrO2给出最低的乙烯选择性。\n\n3. 稳定性：催化剂随时间推移会因碳沉积而失活，不同Cr2O3负载量的催化剂表现出不同的失活速率。\n\n4. Cr2O3负载量：对于SiO2负载的催化剂，乙烷转化率随Cr2O3含量增加而增加，在8 wt.% Cr2O3时达到最大值。\n\n5. 支撑材料性质：氧化物支撑材料的酸碱性强烈影响催化性能，在Cr的固定和分散中起重要作用。\n\n6. 活性位点和机理：表面Cr3+物种和Cr6+/Cr3+偶被认为是乙烷脱氢的活性位点。催化活性取决于催化剂的氧化还原性质。\n\n7. 反应途径：由于CO2的引入，反应涉及脱氢和氧化脱氢两种途径。\n\n优化整体性能的主要挑战和权衡包括：\n- 平衡活性和选择性，例如Cr2O3/ZrO2表现出高活性但低选择性。\n- 优化Cr2O3负载量以最大化转化率同时保持稳定性。\n- 缓解由于碳沉积导致的催化剂失活。\n- 调整催化剂的氧化还原性质和酸碱性以提高性能。\n- 管理平行反应途径（脱氢和氧化脱氢）以获得所需的产物分布。\n\n给定的文献中没有直接讨论CO2分压的影响，这代表了全面优化这些催化剂时可用数据的空白。", "Doi": "10.1016/s0926-860x(99)00450-0"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Many bulk and supported oxide-based materials containing active species, such as Cr (Michorczyk and Ogonowski, 2003; Michorczyk et al., 2008; Michorczyk et al., 2010; Michorczyk et al., 2011), Ga (Michorczyk et al., 2003; Xu et al., 2006), V (Takahara et al., 2005; Ogonowski and Skrzynska, 2008) and Fe (Michorczyk et al., 2004) have been studied as catalysts for dehydrogenation of propane in the presence of CO2.\"\n\n[2] \"The one-step mechanism has been proposed for redox oxides (Cr2O3, Cr2O5, ZnO and V2O5), where CO2 can participate as an oxidizing agent in the following redox cycle\"\n\n[3] \"The two-step pathway has been proposed for non-redox oxides such as Ga2O3 (Xu et al., 2006; Zheng et al., 2005). Production of H2 could be an indication of the two-step pathway.\"\n\n[4] \"Ga2O3 showed drastic deactivation during a few hours on stream (Zheng et al., 2005). Besides coke formation, the reduction of Cr(VI) to Cr(III) is responsible for deactivation of chromium based catalysts (Zhang et al., 2011).\"\n\n[5] \"As a consequence, acidic supports or oxides are not desirable as they favor cracking and coke formation (that is, acid coking (Richardson, 1989)). In fact, basic oxides have been favored for CO2-PDH reaction due to the acidic nature of CO2.\"\n\n[6] \"Basic oxides have been favored for CO2-PDH reaction due to the acidic nature of CO2. However, the alkali and alkaline earth oxides are inefficient because they form carbonate species in the presence of carbon dioxide (Rangel et al., 2012). Metal oxides of moderate basicity are required and must participate in the redox process with the reduction of carbon dioxide (Krylov et al., 1995).\"\n\n[7] \"Unfortunately, depending on the system conditions, many undesired side reactions can occur including dry reforming of propane to synthesis gas\"\n\n[8] \"Propane dehydrogenation with carbon dioxide is characterized by rapid catalyst deactivation due to coke formation.\"", "English": "The literature does not provide comprehensive information on how the specific support materials mentioned (SiO2, MCM-41, H-ZSM-5, Al2O3, ZrO2, and CeO2) influence chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions. However, some general insights can be drawn:\n\n1. Activity and selectivity: Chromium-based catalysts are among the most active and selective for CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation of propane.\n\n2. Reaction mechanism: Chromium oxide catalysts (Cr2O3, Cr2O5) follow a one-step mechanism, where CO2 acts as an oxidizing agent in a redox cycle. This differs from non-redox oxides like Ga2O3, which follow a two-step pathway.\n\n3. Support material considerations: \n   - Acidic supports are undesirable as they promote cracking and coke formation.\n   - Basic oxides are favored due to the acidic nature of CO2.\n   - However, highly basic supports (alkali and alkaline earth oxides) are inefficient due to carbonate formation.\n   - Metal oxides with moderate basicity that can participate in the redox process are preferred.\n\n4. Stability: Major challenges include:\n   - Rapid deactivation due to coke formation.\n   - Reduction of Cr(VI) to Cr(III) in chromium-based catalysts.\n\n5. CO2 partial pressure: While not explicitly discussed, it likely influences:\n   - The oxidative dehydrogenation reaction rate.\n   - Coke removal efficiency.\n   - Potential carbonate formation on certain supports.\n\n6. Side reactions: Undesired reactions like dry reforming of propane can occur depending on system conditions.\n\nKey challenges and trade-offs in optimizing overall performance include:\n1. Balancing activity and stability.\n2. Optimizing support basicity to prevent carbonate formation while promoting the redox process.\n3. Minimizing coke formation and enhancing coke removal without compromising selectivity.\n4. Maintaining the oxidation state of chromium.\n5. Controlling undesired side reactions.\n\nFurther research is needed to understand the specific effects of different support materials and to optimize reaction conditions for chromium oxide catalysts in CO2 oxidative dehydrogenation reactions.", "Chinese": "文献并未提供关于所提及的特定支撑材料（SiO2、MCM-41、H-ZSM-5、Al2O3、ZrO2和CeO2）如何影响二氧化碳氧化脱氢反应中的铬氧化物催化剂的全面信息。然而，可以得出一些一般性见解：\n\n1. 活性和选择性：铬基催化剂是丙烷二氧化碳氧化脱氢反应中最活跃和选择性最高的催化剂之一。\n\n2. 反应机理：铬氧化物催化剂（Cr2O3、Cr2O5）遵循一步机理，其中二氧化碳在氧化还原循环中充当氧化剂。这与非氧化还原氧化物（如Ga2O3）遵循的两步途径不同。\n\n3. 支撑材料考虑：\n   - 酸性支撑材料不受欢迎，因为它们促进裂解和积碳。\n   - 由于CO2的酸性，碱性氧化物受到青睐。\n   - 然而，高度碱性的支撑材料（碱金属和碱土金属氧化物）由于形成碳酸盐而效率低下。\n   - 首选能够参与氧化还原过程的中等碱性金属氧化物。\n\n4. 稳定性：主要挑战包括：\n   - 由于积碳导致的快速失活。\n   - 铬基催化剂中Cr(VI)还原为Cr(III)。\n\n5. CO2分压：虽然没有明确讨论，但可能影响：\n   - 氧化脱氢反应速率。\n   - 积碳去除效率。\n   - 在某些支撑材料上可能形成碳酸盐。\n\n6. 副反应：根据系统条件，可能发生不希望的反应，如丙烷的干重整。\n\n优化整体性能的主要挑战和权衡包括：\n1. 平衡活性和稳定性。\n2. 优化支撑材料的碱度，以防止碳酸盐形成的同时促进氧化还原过程。\n3. 最小化积碳形成并增强积碳去除，同时不影响选择性。\n4. 维持铬的氧化态。\n5. 控制不希望的副反应。\n\n需要进一步研究以了解不同支撑材料的具体影响，并优化二氧化碳氧化脱氢反应中铬氧化物催化剂的反应条件。", "Doi": "10.1080/00986445.2015.1017638"},
